B00DJZR46G|5.0|This millennium in his albums (if not some side projects) Elton has been intent on re-establishing himself as a musical artist to be taken seriously, rather than a declining purveyor of plastic pop and inconsistent albums. He has made good progress; with The Diving Board he has arrived. That is not to say it will suit all Elton fans. Amid the exciting buzz of praise, there have been some dissenting voices. But my own doubts when underwhelmed by first impressions of lead single Home Again and a live version of upbeat Mexican Vacation have been well and truly laid to rest.<br /><br />Don't expect an album full of spectacular tracks, catchy pop, instant classic singles or a return to hard-driving 70s rock. Pared back to central piano-bass-drum trio, with elegant shafts of colour from cellos and horn, The Diving Board's strength comes from its cohesive mix of consistent pleasures- striking piano music, Elton in fine voice and tracks that grow, unfolding their beauty with repeated listens.<br /><br />The Diving Board is a labour of love, which gathers r&b, gospel, jazz and classical influences, with sumptuous and tender ballads, a few upbeat numbers and three brief improvised \\"Dream\\" piano interludes. It may remind at times of the early Elton John and Tumbleweed Connection albums, Blue Moves, Songs from the West Coast and even (superior) hints of Lestat, or what that musical might have been. Yet while it's familiar it's also bold and intriguing- a tremendous cumulative experience for me, rounded off by a sublime title track, that lifted me to places Elton's music hasn't taken me since Captain Fantastic.<br /><br />Yes, this is the Elton album I've waited 38 long years for. It's deep, warm, dark, rich and wonderful.<br /><br />My wife also loves the album and we hope you do too.

0307271609|4.0|Jung Chang's biography of Empress Dowager Cixi (Tzu Hsi)is an ambitious project, as the author attempts to cover the entire life of the empress. It became clear from reading the book that Cixi's life and times were so complex that one single volume can't do her (or China) justice.<br /><br />This book is not an academic history, but a popular history/biography that will appeal to a wide audience. Even if you know nothing about early modern China -- and especially if you don't -- this would be a good first read. Many things happened during Cixi's lifetime: the Opium Wars, the introduction of the railroad and photography, ending foot binding, and Cixi's attempts at forming a Chinese parliament. I found the writing style to be clear.<br /><br />Chang's book answered a lot of questions for me. I am a graduate history student, but my forte is not China. However, I do know something about the Boxer Rebellion and the Opium Wars and the issues with Europeans forcing their way into China. Chang showed me these things from a different vantage point, which was refreshing and gave me some insight into what the Chinese thought about the Europeans. But Chang stopped short of moralizing and presented the history in a pretty straightforward manner.<br /><br />Cixi's life was one of intrigue and power plays, both inside and outside of the Forbidden City. In the early to mid 1800s, China was being influenced by European technology and philosophy. What Chang paints is a complex portrait of how Cixi and other Chinese potentates adopted or adapted or rejected modernization. Cixi comes across as a level-headed, yet strong-willed woman who tried to put the needs of her country first.<br /><br />I have not read very much about the empress before, so I had no particular image in mind when I read this book, but other reviewers noted that Cixi is often depicted as cruel and backward. Chung also mentions that Cixi was not a favorite of Mao or other more recent Chinese politicians, who essentially conducted a smear campaign on Cixi. Whether that was to serve a political or sexist agenda, though, I leave for others to decide. In the end though, Cixi was human, and not all of her decisions worked out well. Cixi died just a few years before World War I.<br /><br />My review copy was a proof that included photographs but no captions, and no bibliography or index. B00DB2JQ7W|5.0|When The Hardest Working Man In Music has a new idea, everyone should pay attention. Warren Haynes has built a career on organizing jams for charity (this December will be the 25th Christmas Jam in Asheville, North Carolina) and for adding his guitar to many established bands (Phil Lesh and friends, The Dead, Dave Matthews among many others).As the leader of Gov't. Mule, Haynes has taken on a very different project: a new album of eleven original tracks, with a second disc featuring different guest vocalists with the Mule supporting them.<br /><br />The album opener, \\"World Boss\\" is typical rocking Mule, but an unexpected chord structure makes the listener take special notice. Great rhythm guitar featured here, due mainly to keyboardist Danny Louis' expanded role as multi-instrumentalist. This track, with the opening line  \\"Have you heard the news\\" reminds one of \\"Bad Man Walking\\" from \\"Deja Voodoo\\" (Hey! can I tell you a little story?\\"). Warren Haynes demands your attention.<br /><br />\\"Whisper In Your Soul\\" has the sound of early Mule (think \\"Temporary Saint\\" from the first album). Drummer Matt Abts is featured on this track, and the inventive bass of  newest member Jorgen Carlsson is equal to that of his predecessors. In fact, one of the highlights of this album is it's SPACE. This is a muscular band that never overplays; each member manages to be heard without crowding the other players.<br /><br />\\"Captured\\" is a showcase for the soulful vocals of Haynes. Being such a virtuoso on guitar, it's hard to remember that his first love starting out was singing. This sounds like a love letter to his wife. Louis' electric piano plays wonderful counterpoint to Haynes' fretwork, and Haynes wrote a cool line that threw me: \\"Never thought I'd love someone more than I love myself\\".<br /><br />\\"Scared To Live\\" is a Reggae flavored number that works. I know that the \\"Mighty<br />High\\" thing wasn't for everybody, but this Haynes/Louis song flows thanks to Louis' keyboards and the masterful drumming of Abts. \\"Stoop So Low\\" is a good old fashioned take on a problematic woman, and the tune contains some great angry lyrics (\\"Remember that time down in Mexico? I knew right then and there I should have let you go\\"). After a few similar verses, the band plays an ascending riff, then doubles the pace for a guitar and organ workout with Delaney and Bonnie inspired vocals by Alecia Chakour and Nigel Hall.<br /><br />\\"Funny Little Tragedy\\" is the best kiss-off since Dylan's \\"Idiot Wind\\". Haynes has featured Louis over the years, but here he is downright encouraging to Louis on guitar. Haynes Announces \\"Danny Louis!\\" right before Louis plays a brief but tasteful solo. A second guitar increases the scope of the newer songs.<br /><br />\\"Bring On The Music\\" is atypical for the Mule. This is a song of optimism, although it has a feeling of foreboding just before Haynes plays an extended solo, one of his best on record. I've read where Haynes' playing here is a tribute to Paul Kosoff. Perhaps, but to my ears this sounds like the Warren Haynes that played with the masterful Dickey Betts; in fact, he channels Betts right before the end of the song which ends slowly, each musician adding a small flourish at the end. It's as if they don't want the song to end.<br /><br />The second disc also starts off with \\"World Boss\\". Ben Harper was born to sing this song; add some world class harp from Charlie Musselwhite and this track would be right at home on the recent Harper/Musselwhite collaboration \\"Get Up!\\". \\"Funny Little Tragedy\\"-I never imagined Elvis Costello with the mule, but hey-it works! Just looking at Costello's recent pairings (The Roots, Allen Toussaint ) one shouldn't be surprised. Costello obviously plays well with others. He also introduces Danny Louis before the guitar solo.<br /><br />This is the track that kills! \\"Stoop So Low\\" features the great Dr. John, and you know we're in for a treat from the get-go when he starts the number with a devious little chuckle. The good Doc only gets better through the years, offering that special brand of voodoo only he do so well. You'll crack up when Doc growls softly \\"How can you stoop so mother f-----g low?\\" right before Haynes and company jam in a very jazzy fashion-very different from the Mule's version.<br /><br />Toots Hibbert (another ubiquitous musician) brings authenticity to \\"Scared To Live\\". Carlsson and Abts drive this track with more organ and electric piano from Louis. \\"Bring On The Music\\" features Ty Taylor of the great young band Vintage Trouble. Taylor's phrasing is very similar to Haynes'. Although this track is over three minutes shorter than the first disc's version, it's a highlight of the album.<br /><br />\\"Forsaken Savior\\" features Dave Matthews at the mic, and I did a double take when I first heard it. This does not sound like the Matthews we're all familiar with. Here he sounds earnest and very direct.I actually prefer the guitar solo here to the one on the first disc. \\"When The World Gets Small\\" features one of the most unique singers of all time, Steve Winwood. One of his trademarks is to deliver some passages quietly, then rise in volume when you're \\"leaning in\\" to listen. Choosing Winwood to close out the disc was a smart decision on Haynes' part.<br /><br />The concept of having guest vocalists record a companion disc on a new release is a great one . I don't believe this has been done before, at least not in the spirit of Gov't Mule's \\"Shout!\\". Think of the possibilities-Terry Hanck adding his sax and singing to a Rod Piazza project, or Selwyn Birchwood contributing to a Buddy Guy release. Hope the labels are paying attention.

B00E66QPCG|3.0|This book is for all the readers who want a successful trader to share a specific, quantified system, well, here you go. The book shares a day trading strategy based primarily on trading the futures market for the benefit of leverage but can also be used for stocks and ETFs. He uses bollinger bands, MACD, and ADR for a intra-day trend trading strategy. He explains that this system requires a daily trend to be profitable and shoots for a 1:1.5 risk/reward ratio so it is profitable even if 50% of the trades are losers. It becomes much more profitable with a 60% win rate, Many new traders do not understand that the key to profitable trading is simple bigger wins than losses. The author uses profit targets to close his winning trades and generally only gets one signal to trade per day on average. This would be a good book for those that have the basics of day trading down and want a specific strategy, and even if you do not use his it could give you ideas for building and creating your own.

B001QJUX24|5.0|I was six years old when I saw this film with my parents during its initial release. Needless to say it left a lasting impression with me. The Searchers is one of \\"the Duke's\\" finest performances in the prime of a great acting career and is well worth a place in any DVD library. The action and realism are a bit dated compared to today's standards but was state of the art for the mid-1950's. Yet, the scenery, filming locations, and cinematography are timeless. The only real issue I have with the film is the use of anachronistic weapons depicted for the historical period. The film is supposed to take place from 1868 thru 1873. However, most of the weaponry shown in the film was from a later time period. Throughout the film the main characters use 1873 Colt Army or shorter barrel versions of the same pistol, and the Winchester lever action rifles look like the 1892 version. Perhaps I'm just being \\"picky\\", but it seems to me at best the pistols of the period would have been a 1860 Colt or 1858 Remington conversion from cap and ball to cartridge, and the Winchesters would have been the 1866 model. Yet, the historical inaccuracy does not diminish the fact that this film is one of the great definitive westerns.  I also highly recommend the book by Alan LeMay which has a much better ending than the film (no spoiler intended), however the film is a very good adaptation. Watch the film and then read the book and you will not be disappointed.

B00DJ80VLS|5.0|When A Dramatic Turn of Events was released, I and many other people were pleasantly surprised at the well-executed trip back to their roots. Not knowing what to expect of this album, I was slightly skeptical after hearing the two singles, \\"The Enemy Inside\\" (Heavy, technical and fast paced) and \\"Along for the Ride\\" (Slow proggy ballad). But that skepticism quickly changed to joy the moment I popped the CD in my stereo and pressed play.<br /><br />The album opens with a short instrumental score that emits shades of Six Degrees. Brilliantly composed and a great way to start off such an epic album. (4/5)<br /><br />It then moves on to \\"The Enemy Inside\\" which is a song that most people would probably expect out of Dream Theater. It is clearly influenced by their own more modern style of progressive metal. (4/5)<br /><br />After \\"The Enemy Inside\\" comes \\"The Looking Glass\\". At first listen of that Rush-influenced, Images and Words style intro, I could not wipe the smile off my face.  This is also the first song where Myung's bass is very prevalent and noticeable. That is a quality that has been lacking in recent years for Dream Theater. (5/5)<br /><br />\\"Enigma Machine\\" is Dream Theater's first stand alone instrumental to appear on an LP in 10 years (Train of Thought). In between that span of time, they released a single titled \\"Raw Dog\\" for God of War 3. \\"Enigma Machine\\" starts off with a mellow intro but gives you the hint that something big is coming, and sure enough you get blasted with some Petrucci punches seconds later. This is not their best instrumental by any means but it fits the album well. What I enjoyed the most are the flashes of Erotomania. (5/5)<br /><br />The intro of \\"The Bigger Picture\\" makes it seem as if it is going to be a carbon copy of \\"Outcry\\" from A Dramatic Turn of Events, but that soon disappears as James LaBrie starts singing along with a beautiful Rudess piano piece. Afterwards one of the most catchy choruses of the album ensues. Althoughthis is one of the more generic songs on the album, it surprises first listeners with quite the epic outro. (4/5)<br /><br />Behind the Veil is one of my personal favorites on the album. The intro sounds like something out of an epic video game or movie followed by one of the heaviest and richest Petrucci licks of Dream Theater history. LaBrie also outdoes himself in this particular piece, mixing vocal styles from many eras of the band. (5/5)<br /><br />\\"Surrender to Reason\\" is  the second song on the album that immediately gives you a Rush/Images and Word vibe. Throughout the song, there are prog licks galore accompanied by another brilliant LaBrie performance. My personal favorite part of the song is the absolutely monstrous and blistering instrumental section about 4 minutes in. A slick Myung bassline and a brilliant solo by Petrucci. I just wish it lasted longer. (5/5)<br /><br />\\"Along for the Ride\\" was the second single they released after \\"The Enemy Inside\\". It is a simple (by Dream Theater standards) prog ballad with flashes of good, but for the most part it is fairly generic. The lyrics are quite moving to anyone trying to relate though. (4/5)<br /><br />Finally, the song we have all been waiting for since it was announced. The next Dream Theater epic. \\"Illumination Theory\\" starts with an epic orchestral/rock theme that recurs later in the song through a full blown orchestral score. Soon followed by probably my new favorite Petrucci riff of all time. I just could not refrain from head banging at first listen. After the introduction to the themes (Paradoxe de la Lumiere Noire) of the song comes the first vocal section of the song (Live, Die, Kill). Afterwards comes the brilliant orchestral score  with REAL strings nonetheless. It is quite a moving piece. Soon afterwards comes my favorite part of the song and the album. When the orchestral score subsides, the listener gets surprised by some drum n' bass followed by some EXPLOSIVE James LaBrie vocals. He hitssome notes I had no idea he was even capable of hitting anymore at this point in this career. Next comes the first full blown instrumental section of the song with flashes of ELP. Also one of the intro theme riffs is refrained at this point underneath Petrucci and Rudess solos. After the outro the song seems as if it may have ended prematurely to some listeners, but there is about 30 seconds of silence until we get the closure we need. An absolutely enlightening and beautiful piano and guitar score that fades out to end off the album. (6/5)<br /><br />Overall I personally thing this is Dream Theaters best work BY FAR since Scenes from a Memory. It has bits of inspiration from every Dream Theater era and even from some other bands. It is easily more innovative and original than anything they have done since Octavarium. I do not take sides in the Portnoy vs Mangini flame war, but this album absolutely proves that Dream Theater can move on just fine without Portnoy. The only \\"bad\\" thing about this album to me is the production and mix of Mangini's kit. His snare sounds horrendous at times. I guess that is one thing Portnoy probably does better than Mangini. Overall I easily score this album a 5 out of 5. Absolutely brilliant, and if you have not bought it or listened to it yet, I highly recommend it.

B002QE3CTY|5.0|First of all, I enjoyed _The Hunger Games_ quite a bit and for a long time was on the lookout for books with dystopian themes to satisfy my lust for futuristic settings and terrifying alternate realities. And I'd been through a lot of duds before I picked up The Maze Runner.<br /><br />Which, while I believe it would qualify as a dystopian novel, didn't satisfy that lust in the way that I had hoped, mainly because this book couldn't be much more different from the aforementioned series except in as much as the main characters are teenagers.<br /><br />I absolutely loved _The Maze Runner_, which I found to be a memorable novel that so far has haunted me and, I'll admit, given me nightmares. And I'm a thirty-four year old woman!<br /><br />This book has received five stars from me because Amazon makes star ratings personal. Five stars means that I loved this book. And because I did, I've rated it five stars.<br /><br />But there are some problems with the novel that I feel need to be addressed for those who are looking for something to read. It's only fair to tell you I loved _The Maze Runner_, was thrilled by _The Scorch Trials_ and detested _The Death Cure_.<br /><br />To start with, the language is very jarring. You'll get used to it as you progress through the trilogy but there were moments I didn't feel that it was worth it to keep trying. By the time the series was over I found myself using phrases like \\"shuck it\\" in my own everyday language. You get used to it, but it's not comfortable in the beginning, and may keep the reader off-pace with the book even as the series progresses. Whatever reason Dashner felt this was a good idea, he needs to rethink his position on trying to be Shakespearean: He isn't, by any stretch of the imagination. We should leave the invention of new words to The Bard.<br /><br />None of the characters were particularly well-developed, and I found it odd how easy it was to dislike Teresa, and in retrospect, Alby. I felt like we should have known more about Frypan (throughout the series, actually) but never got quite enough about him, or about Ben's experiences. I wanted more from Chuck, and for the love of all things holy, THOMAS. I can only hope that D. O'Brien brings something to his role when he portrays the character in the movie.<br /><br />I probably haven't convinced you that this book deserves five stars, so let me try.<br /><br />The story drags you through, if you can get past the first chapter and the confusion about the box, Gally, Alby and Newt (and the long succession of names). There are moments that I experienced real terror, times I couldn't close my eyes without seeing the grievers, or the maze, or the Glade. I can still picture the Glade in my minds eye so clearly, and I believe that part of the beauty of this book (and _The Scorch Trials_) is that Dashner gives readers just enough information about the setting for them to build a vision of it in their own minds.<br /><br />I love setting. I'm a sucker for setting. Atmosphere is everything to me when I'm reading a book. I can get around poor characterization if the atmosphere is great, and I felt this book (and its immediate sequel).<br /><br />If you're someone who reads for atmosphere, you may like this book. B00DG86ARK|5.0|Universal is a concert recording by the British band Anathema, released in 2013 on K Scope records. The concert was shot in support of the band's Weather Systems album at the Ancient Theater of Phillipopolis, Bulgaria on the 22nd of September featuring the Plovdiv Philharmonic Orchestra. The concert was shot while the band were in support of their Weather Systems album from 2012 and their setlist draws heavily from both it, and the previous two full-length studio albums We're Here Because We're Here and A Natural Disaster.<br /><br />The performance is of a very high quality, delivering equally well on the energetic sections of songs, and the shimmering, beautiful quiet sections. The astounding vocal trio of Vincent Cavanagh, Daniel Cavanagh and Lee Douglas, both blend and then contrast their vocal styles to great effect, the rest of the musicians deliver everything with both precision and passion and the Orchestra provide color and texture, really filling out the sound.<br /><br />The mixing job is pretty much perfect and all the instruments are arguably balanced as well as they would be on a studio album, with only the added humanity felt in the vocal and drumming performances giving away that it's a live affair.<br /><br />The visuals are great, with a tasteful stage show in the beautiful ancient theater, a subtle light show and the Orchestra to draw your eye when the band aren't moving much. The camera work and editing is slow and musician-friendly, letting you get a good look at what people are playing rather than zooming frantically from one shot to another every second.<br /><br />The track listing for the main show is as follows: `Untouchable Parts 1&2,' `Thin Air,' `Dreaming Light,' `Lightning Song,' `The Storm Before The Calm,' `Everything,' `A Simple Mistake,' `The Beginning And The End,' `Universal,'  `Closer,' `A Natural Disaster,' `Deep,' `One Last Goodbye,' `Flying,' `Fragile Dreams,' `Panic,' `Emotional Winter/Wings Of God,' `Internal Landscapes' `Fragile Dreams (Reprise)'<br /><br />The bonus feature included is a set of five tracks taken from the stripped down, A Night At The Union Chapel concert, the track listing for which is as follows: `Kingdom' `Thin Air' `Angels Walk Among Us' `A Natural Disaster' `Fragile Dreams.' This feature is similarly well recorded, mixed and edited and no simple throw-away. There are some tracks repeated from the main feature, but their alternative, more unplugged (not completely, but close) style makes it worth having both versions.<br /><br />The Blu-Ray comes in a slim case with a booklet full of photos and the credits. The visuals are NTSC. The main menu only features play and track selection options, and there are no alternative audio (or subtitle) options which may upset some viewers, however I personally was incredibly happy with the audio provided as standard. There are other editions available, for example on Burning Shed  with more extensive features, such as a CD of the audio, but as a cheap and simple version of the main concert, this edition certainly delivers it.<br /><br />Overall, I'm very satisfied with this well made and well performed, good looking and good sounding Blu-Ray Anathema concert, and as long as you like the band and don't have an issue with the lack of audio options, or the setlist, then I highly recommend picking up a copy.agile Dreams (Reprise)'<br /><br />The bonus feature included is a set of five tracks taken from the stripped down, A Night At The Union Chapel concert, the track listing for which is as follows: `Kingdom' `Thin Air' `Angels Walk Among Us' `A Natural Disaster' `Fragile Dreams.' In Twelve Months of a Soviet Childhood: Short Stories author Julia Gousseva transports us behind the iron curtain to a time of innocence in the life of a young girl. Gousseva has given us a vibrant portrayal of what it was really like, and it was not as different or awful as one might think (at least for a child or from their perspective).<br /><br />I like how she took us through a \\"typical\\" year of a Soviet childhood - each story takes place in a different month. The length of each tale is great, allowing for brief reads or allowing us to run through many months at once. It makes me want to collect similar books about growing up in other countries. In the meantime start with this one, it's charming.

B008JFUN6E|2.0|In 2009, out of the scrapped Halo movie, first-time director Neill Blomkamp shocked the world with District 9, a very unique film about extraterrestrial refugees stuck in contemporary South Africa. It currently holds a 90% fresh rating on Rotten Tomatoes, citing its unique story (a rarity in films these days), excellent acting, writing, and (despite its modest budget) special effects. Naturally, expectations were high for his follow up, Elysium. After viewing Blomkamp's second film, one wonders whether he was pressed for time, because it plays out like a first draft in need of heavy revision.<br /><br />In the year 2154, the ultra wealthy live on Elysium, a utopian space station where crime, sickness, and war are nonexistent. Everyone else is stuck on an overpopulated, impoverished earth. One man, however, has the means to change all of that and bring equality to the two worlds.<br /><br />There isn't a singular flaw that can be attributed to Elysium's catastrophic failure, but \\"absolutely no character development\\" is towards the top of the list. Our protagonist, Max (played by Matt Damon) is an ex-con who's trying to stay on the \\"straight and narrow\\". It's difficult to care about him because he is essentially a cardboard cutout, like every character in this movie. The squalor the earthlings live in is portrayed with excellent, stark imagery, but viewers need more than imagery to stay invested in the \\"good\\" characters and their plight. \\"Why should we root for Max? What makes him so special?\\" It's unfortunate that Blomkamp doesn't answer these questions.<br /><br />Some of the characters are an extreme hindrance to the success of the film. Jodie Foster plays Delacourt, Elysium's cruel, scheming Secretary of Defense who has a penchant for poor acting including, but not limited to, cringe-inducing lines unbecoming of a two-time academy award winning actress. Kruger (played by Sharlto Copley of District 9 fame) is meant to be a fun-to-watch villain, but Delacourt's personal mercenary has an incredibly obnoxious, pseudo-French/cockney accent that would be hilarious in a Monty Python movie, but it's distracting and less than intimidating in this one. The actors are not entirely to blame; it's difficult for a good actor/actress to perform well when given poor lines.<br /><br />The environments, spaceships, robots, and weapons are a visual treat, as expected. The action scenes have inventive elements, but they are too few and far between, often relying heavily on slow-motion. Ultimately, the film lacks character development and substance, both of which are essential for the kind of story Blomkamp is trying to tell.<br /><br />Considering how great District 9 was, and the enormous potential Elysium had, it's obvious Blomkamp has some great ideas; it's just a matter of allowing them to develop. 4/10

B00DJZR46G|5.0|To start, \\"The Diving Board\\" is a great success and very much worth a purchase (in \\"deluxe\\" long-form if possible). To expand, since \\"Songs From the West Coast\\" at the turn of the millennium, Elton John has moved in an encouraging direction with his studio album output. His work between 1976 and 2000 was, depending on where one might cherry-pick: mediocre, brilliant, crassly commercial, directionless, or uneven. The highs were actually still as high as during the first seven years of his career, but the lows were much lower indeed. More significantly, the lesser work popped up at a much more alarming rate during this long stretch.<br /><br />The aforementioned direction Elton John now is taking has led to efforts that almost completely remove those lows from his offerings. \\"Peachtree Road\\" was as uneven as they've come in the last twelve years, and it was still, at least, a decent album overall with some specifically fine tracks. His material in the new millennium has continued to trend toward fully-realized work with notable consistency and craftsmanship. Elton John has used each album as a vehicle to rekindle or reconnect with a past sound lost since his peak commercial and artistic years. While he has succeeded marvelously at bringing back a sense of excellence and quality, he has, until now, not done much more artistically than seek to recreate a sound he already had created.<br /><br />Now, however, with \\"The Diving Board\\", he has taken that next step that so many fans and critics have been waiting for. The new album is just as adventurous and risky as \\"Blue Moves\\", but, one would could argue, lacks even one track that could be considered a dud. To extend the metaphor from above, the highs on this album never reach the heights of his greatest songs, but, there are also no lows. \\"The Diving Board\\" is unpredictable, amusing, understated, learned, and even, nearly, avant-garde! A few listens through will reveal the hooks for which Elton John is so deservedly famous; the first time through will not be enough in this case. Patience will reward the listener though; his best songs have always been those that take a while to hum because they are complicated enough that once you have them, they don't annoy you two days later (like with most hook-driven pop material). Elton John has finally taken his new consistency and moved it forward without trying to capitalize on taking it back (even if the marketing for this album is unsurprisingly claiming otherwise). \\"Rolling Stone\\" gave this album four stars out of five, which, on their rating scale, translates to \\"excellent\\". I would tend to concur. However, Amazon's four star review translates to \\"like\\"; its five star review to \\"love\\". On this rating scale, I am more in the five-star camp (hence my choice). Still, though this album is probably his greatest work since Ford was president, he does have it in him to take this renaissance to an even more brilliant level. I very sincerely hope he continues in this direction. One or two more albums like this, along with his work after \\"The Road to El Dorado\\", would lead to a strong case that Elton John as an album auteur may be a greater artist now than he ever actually was before.

B00A6CCF0K|4.0|Decades after fleeing the horrors of the Overlook Hotel, Danny Torrance and a psychic girl band join forces to banish an evil entity that seeks to steal their very souls.<br /><br />Two years after he and his mother WENDY fled the Overlook Hotel after the accident that killed his father, Danny walks into the bathroom of the small apartment he shares with his mother and sees Mrs. Massey, the dead woman he first saw in room 217 of the hotel. He tells his mother not to go into the bathroom and then clams up. Concerned, she calls Dick Halloran, the man whose \\"powerful hunch\\" caused him to turn up at the Overlook in time to save her and Danny.<br /><br />Like Danny, Dick has \\"the shining,\\" and he teaches Danny a technique for literally locking the horrors away in his mind. That trick works for the visitations but not for the memories and in the present, Danny is a just-barely-functioning alcoholic haunted by a crime he committed years ago, stealing money from a party-loving single mother named Deenie.<br /><br />Meanwhile, in another part of the country, a group that calls itself the TRUE KNOT is making its nomadic way toward New York where they intend to feed on the spiritual \\"steam\\" given off by those who have the Shining, a steam that is released at their death. The cult's leader, a dangerous beauty called Rose, knows that something horrible is going to happen in New York and promises everyone a feast.<br /><br />At the same time, a young girl named Abra is growing up, and as the story unfolds, the trajectories of these three characters are about to cross. By the time Abra's a teenager, Danny is working at a hospice where he is called \\"Doctor Sleep\\" because he has the knack for helping the patients die. Rose is aware of both Danny and Abra and knows they both have abundant steam.<br /><br />This is the long-awaited sequel to Stephen King's novel THE SHINING and although it's not absolutely necessary to be familiar with the earlier book, it helps. On the other hand, readers who are TOO familiar with King's work may find this book is a little ... familiar. (In particular, the Teenytown segment of the book will remind King's fans of parts of JOYLAND and it's likely this book and JOYLAND were written at mostly the same time.) Also the grown-up Danny Torrance has a lot in common with the hero of THE DEAD ZONE, particularly in the way he can intuit so much from a simple touch. Not only that, but in concept the True Knot remind us a lot of the vampiric aliens in Tobe Hooper's LIFEFORCE and the silvery mist of STEAM is not unlike the cloud of life force that the aliens use to replenish themselves in that movie. (And of course, Dan's team reminds us a bit of the team of children/adults who go after the evil that is Pennywise in the novel/movie IT.)<br /><br />King is the KING of character creation, and the steps he takes to establish the three main characters go back to all their childhoods. The way Abra and Danny connect is through Danny's imaginary friend Tony (readers of THE SHINING will remember Tony) and it makes perfect sense that the two can connect psychically. Abra's talent is INTENSE and she shows up on Rose's radar almost from the moment of her birth. Rose and looks forward to plucking Abra's steam, but she tells her consort, Crow Daddy, that she'll let her \\"ripen\\" a bit longer. (All the members of the True Knot have names they call themselves among themselves and then what they call \\"rube names\\" for dealing with ordinary people.)<br /><br />The idea of the nomadic band of the True Knot is intriguing. They're like gypsy \\"travelers\\" as they move from town to town except that they have tremendous financial resources (almost a billion) stashed away in caches of diamonds and art and bonds and so forth. Rose is a bit like Randall Flagg, the villain in THE STAND in the way she calls followers to her band and the way she wants to take their \\"steam\\" the way Randall took souls. King incorporates 9/11 into the story in a way that's incredibly chilling, and he uses it to show Abra's talent in a way that makes sense but also horrifies us. (Abra's father's reaction to her powers is complicated and also realistic.)<br /><br />There are some incredibly moving moments in this story, particularly when Dan is helping one of the \\"guests\\" at the hospice die. (Those scenes are almost signature Stephen King scenes and after all this time, he's really, really, really good at them.) But the narrative here is extremely episodic and as with THE STAND, it follows a couple of people on parallel tracks for a LONG time. Once we get to the meat of the story and the final confrontation draws hear, the pace of the story picks up and the plot becomes more important. Still, as the saying goes, it's not the destination that's important, it's the journey. B00F2LIV4E|5.0|Dream Theater has been a favorite band of mine since Images and Words.  Since then I have managed to get every release that has come out and even hunted down their first album prior to Labrie and even their Majesty stuff.  With that being said, I am a fan of DT and have eagerly awaited their new release with Mangini being fully involved this time.  And by no means did they disappoint.  Since Portnoy's departure, it seems that DT's music and writing creativity has become cohesive again and looks like they have a creative flow that keeps getting better.  I was worried when Portnoy left at the time, thinking this might be it for DT, but lucky for all us fans, that hasn't happened.  Don't get me wrong, I liked Portnoy with the band but I do feel that he kind of gave the band a raw deal with his hopping out of the band to go to what he thinks is his next gig with Avenged Sevenfold, only to get kicked out and then almost beg to come back.  I bet he does want to come back now after a Grammy nomination.<br /><br />DT is one of the few bands that I have seen in concert that sound as good live if not better than their albums.  They always bring a musical majesty to their concerts that leave you blown away.  With that being said, this album does a great job at bringing that awe-inspired feeling like I get when I watch them live.<br /><br />The album starts off the \\"False Awakening Suite,\\"  which is a reminder of the \\"Overture\\" opening in the Six Degrees of Inner Turbulence.  There may be other prog metal bands that blend guitar riffs, drums and keyboards but no one does it better than DT.<br /><br />The songs `Behind the Veil,' `The Looking Glass' and `Along for the Ride' all give you moments to remind you of where DT was influenced.  Close you eyes and you can almost hear the sound of Rush coming through your speakers.  These songs have their own uniqueness and instantly drew me into the album.<br /><br />The album surprisingly features tunes that could be heard playing on rock radio, but that isn't a knock on the album as the song have great lyrics and catchy melodies.  If you think that the band is forgetting what made them great in years past then listen to the single, `The Enemy Inside,' which give you a crash course on the band and llisten to the epic 22 minute Illumination Theory which will remind you of what DT is all about.<br /><br />Illumination theory like other epics that DT has created in years past is broken down into parts: i. Paradoxe de la Lumi&egrave;re Noire, ii. Live, Die, Kill, iii. The Embracing Circle, iv. The Pursuit of Truth, v. Surrender, Trust & Passion.  For the fans like me that love these epic songs, Illumination theory brings you a jam-packed with a head-spinning mix of quiet interludes, face melting jams and, courtesy of bassist Myung and Mangini, rhythmic magic.  An almost album within an album.  Then, as simply as it began, it ends - quiet and peacefully making me sit back and go wow and ask for more.  DT always pushes its creativity into something new and they don't disappoint here but they also at the same time bring you something familiar like that comfortable couch you have had since college.  The band also seems to be expanding their appeal with catchy melodies and lyrics as well.  Like the song from my favorite song on the album says, \\"I believe I am along for the ride\\"  and I say hell yea, I am just enjoying the scenery.<br /><br />From top to bottom, this is a great album.  DT seems to be moving from the Portnoy era and creating a legacy on their own that is distinct yet still what we have all come to know and love as DT.  Is a grammy nod in the card for this album? I don't know, and frankly that doesn't make or break DT but it would be a great way for the band to say Take that Portnoy. B00DJZR46G|4.0|As a musician Elton John is best remembered for his many memorable singles spanning from the early 1970s to the present.  He is not often associated with consistent and memorable albums bar a few.  While some of his albums have been truly memorable, most have not been arranged by a common theme and often are a grab bag of songs of varying quality.  You can't really blame Elton for that as he's not the lyricist...that's Bernie Taupin...and he has to work with the material he's handed.  Many of his albums are completely enjoyable and some of the non-single album tracks have become fan favorites you'll hear in concert.  As of late Elton's output has deliberately slowed down, focusing on quality rather than quantity and some of his recent albums have been quite good and reflective of that emphasis.  It's hard to believe it's been almost seven years since his last solo outing on [[ASIN:B000H7JDVI The Captain and the Kid]] and in that time he did a staggeringly great album with longtime friend Leon Russell [[ASIN:B003TWP5JC The Union]], and here Elton again taps producer T-Bone Burnett to helm.  It is Burnett who made the audacious suggestion to ditch his usual backing band and return to the piano, bass and drums format from his earliest albums; a daring and stripped down approach for an artist whose mantra could easily be \\"more is more!\\"  But the approach initially yielded somewhat unsatisfying results for Elton, a demanding perfectionist, which resulted in producing new songs, revamping the tracks to fit a theme.  Well...after all that fussing and twiddling we're left with the final product...so how is it?<br /><br />The answer is gorgeous and a bit muddled, thematic but uneven.  The songs here are quite good and grow with repeated listening, but the sequencing is a bit odd and haphazard as some tracks harmonize better together than others.  Nothing here is going to scream [[ASIN:B000001EG8 Empty Sky]] but you'll hear faint echoes of \\"Tumbleweed Connection\\" and other eras in Elton's past.  But overall \\"The Diving Board is a brave step forward into the unknown, something the lyrics touch on intermittently.  \\"The Diving Board\\" opens with \\"Oceans Away\\", a gorgeous piano opening, solo voice and piano and very poignant lyrics about aging.  Stripped down to the bare essentials, it's an insight into how to survive and thrive in life, transitions, how we have to give up what we leave behind.  At once profound and deep, it's easily the best track on the album.  \\"Oscar Wilde Gets Out\\" is as much about Oscar Wilde as it is resisting conformity, speaking truth to power, and being who you are.  Subject matter appropriate for Elton at this stage of his life.  At this point it seems \\"The Diving Board\\" is hitting its stride, touching on subjects of identity and place when it shifts into \\"A Town Called Jubilee\\" and \\"The Ballad of Blind Tom\\", but of which would sound right on [[ASIN:B000001EG4 Tumbleweed Connection]] but 40 years on they're a bit too corn pone and stereotypical for latter-day Elton and it just doesn't seem to fit with the rest of the tracks.  Granted they would have sounded great on [[ASIN:B003TWP5JC The Union]] but here they're jarring and discordant.<br /><br />\\"My Quicksand\\" is more in keeping with the bulk of the tracks, pointing out how bipolar the album is.  This is another standout track that is quite lovely and looking back on his life. \\"Can't Stay Alone Tonight\\" points to the type of filler you typically get on some of Elton's albums.  A nice song but forgettable.  \\"Voyeur\\" was initially supposed to be the title track for this album, another nice introspective track that fits thematically as does \\"Home Again\\", the leadoff single, and \\"Take This Dirty Water.\\"  Harkening back to his earliest albums \\"Dream #2\\" is a beautiful and brief musical interlude blending into \\"The New Fever Waltz\\" a track very reminiscent of \\"Oceans Away\\" with more musings on life; another great track.  \\"Mexican Vacation (Kids in the Candlelight)\\", thesecond single is a bit of honkytonk that wouldn't have been out of place on his album with Leon Russell.  Not a bad song at all, far closer to \\"A Town\\" and \\"Ballad of Blind Tom\\" which points out the scattershot nature of the album. Some tracks sound more similar to others and others should have been left out entirely as the dissimilarities in tracks can be at times jarring and will make listeners question \\"what is this albums supposed to be?\\"  \\"Dream #3\\" is a faster tempo interlude designed as an intro for \\"The Diving Board.\\"  The title track is a nice compromise between some of the faster tempo songs and slower ballads and again features some great piano work.  Elton is again looking back on his life and the chances and risks he took...a nice coda for a thoroughly enjoyable album.  Is it as good as some of his recent ones, like [[ASIN:B000H7JDVI The Captain and the Kid]], [[ASIN:B00061X95Q Peachtree Road]] and [[ASIN:B00005NZDW Songs from the West Coast]]?  Yes and no.  It is undeniably different than those albums and also not as strong.  Some of the tracks here would have been best omitted for better consistency.  Without his normal backing band Elton still sounds great and is pushing the envelope exploring ground not previously  attempted in quite a while.  To a large degree he succeeds, creating an intimate and personal album not really done since [[ASIN:B0000089F2 The One]] or [[ASIN:B000001EDN Made In England]].  This is a high risk/potentially high reward album for Elton and if I were a betting man, I would bet this is going to succeed!second single is a bit of honkytonk that wouldn't have been out of place on his album with Leon Russell.  Not a bad song at all, far closer to \\"A Town\\" and \\"Ballad of Blind Tom\\" which points out the scattershot nature of the album. Some tracks sound more similar to others and others should have been left out entirely as the dissimilarities in tracks can be at times jarring and will make listeners question \\"what is this albums supposed to be?\\"  \\"Dream #3\\" is a faster tempo interlude designed as an intro for \\"The Diving Board.\\"  The title track is a nice compromise between some of the faster tempo songs and slower ballads and again features some great piano work.  Elton is again looking back on his life and the chances and risks he took...a nice coda for a thoroughly enjoyable album. B00EDK1LP6|4.0|\\"Pacific Rim\\" has become one of my favorite movies in recent memory, a thrilling blockbuster sci-fi smash-fest that nonetheless manages to have well-rounded characters and a strong heart beneath it's iron-and-titanium exterior.  I fell in love with the film and its world, and eagerly await its DVD release date.  I even splurged on its art book (which has sadly been backordered until December), and when I received the soundtrack as a gift from a friend I was rather stupidly excited.  Movie music is a great way to relive one's favorite moments from a film, and I wanted to be able to indulge in some of my favorite movie moments even when away from the screen.<br /><br />The \\"Pacific Rim\\" soundtrack may not be as memorable and iconic as John William's work, nor is it quite as gripping and emotionally charged as the \\"Transformers\\" musical score.  But it's still a fun and epic collection in its own right.<br /><br />Composed by the man behind the \\"Iron Man\\" score, the soundtrack of this film is a fusion of orchestral music and guitar/electronica elements, similar to the aforementioned \\"Iron Man.\\"  It has it's own epic riff, a six-note motif that crops up throughout the soundtrack and always seems to be an indication of something big going down (quite similar to how \\"The Imperial March\\" always meant bad news in the \\"Star Wars\\" movies).  And it's not afraid to experiment with different styles for different situations, and to come up with its own tone and themes to suit different characters.<br /><br />Favorite tracks include:<br /><br />\\"Pacific Rim\\" -- definitely the main theme and the most well-known of the film, this is an epic number that pops up thematically throughout the soundtrack.<br /><br />\\"Cancelling the Apocalypse\\" -- surprisingly low-key, but a good thoughtful number that underscores a serious moment of the film.<br /><br />\\"2500 Tons of Awesome\\" and \\"Call Me Newt\\" -- quirky but fun numbers that befit one of the more comedic characters of the film<br /><br />\\"Double Event\\" and \\"Category 5\\" -- definite \\"bad news\\" numbers, these are reminiscent of the soundtracks of the old Godzilla and other giant monster movies.  The homage is quite fitting.<br /><br />\\"Hannibal Chau\\" -- this number has an exotic, oriental flare, and has a slightly darker undertone befitting one of the more sinister characters of the film.<br /><br />While not the best movie soundtrack I've ever had the pleasure of hearing, the \\"Pacific Rim\\" soundtrack is still epic and exciting, and a nice blend of traditional orchestra and electronic instrumentation, quite fitting for the film's blend of mechanical titan vs. organic monster action.  If you liked the \\"Transformers\\" or \\"Iron Man\\" scores, you need to give \\"Pacific Rim\\" a listen. B00D7OXUIK|3.0|I was fortunate enough to get this disc a day in advance of its official release when I was starting a week of holiday. I have had time to listen to it all at least twice.<br /><br />If you are looking for this music with the keyboard part played on piano, there are not many choices. The reason is that it does not seem to work well --- compare to the Goldberg Variations, a piece that seems to bloom on every keyboard instrument and in arrangements for non-keyboard instruments.<br /><br />These two discs contain the six sonatas for violin and keyboard accompaniment, and they are presented here in the usual order, numerically increasing in the BWV catalog, and b, A, E, c, f, G by keys. Liner notes are the usual almost non-existent ECM fare, with only tracks, timings and few beautiful photographs of the recording sessions.<br /><br />The out-of-print Mela Tenenbaum & Richard Kapp collaboration on ESS.A.Y is the only piano and violin version in my collection, and I have had it since its issue. I bought it primarily to have contrast in my collection, and to see how this music endured the transition to modern performance. The consensus opinion of many reviewers has been \\"no so well,\\" although the reasons have to do with many things other than the transition from harpsichord to piano.<br /><br />A discussion of the sound is a good place to start. Makarski and Jarrett are LOUD, and that is not a good thing to say about music that is somewhat starved for dynamic range in almost all performances that have made it to the recording stage. I was originally concerned that the piano / violin balance might tilt to the keyboard, but if that was also your concern you have no need of further worry.<br /><br />Unusually for ECM, the recording contains no sense of the vast space shown in the photos of the venue. The recording is airless and clinical, a particularly abrasive characteristic during the intimate moments of the music. In the fast movements, Makarski and Jarrett just pound it out so hard that the sound seems to come directly from the speakers. I was disappointed by the recording, and it is even worse on headphones.<br /><br />For performance, a comparison with Tenenbaum and Kapp seems to be a logical beginning. At this point, we enter the dreaded mixed bag of characteristics. Makarski plays more \\"accurately\\" than does Tenenbaum, and Jarrett is as accurate as anyone, regardless of what he is playing. But Makarski's instrument is harsh in its sound, and it is always at the front of the duo.<br /><br />Specifics? Listen to the opening of the A major sonata (Track 5 on Disc 1). This is a reverie of Bach's, and it is played at a typical and acceptable tempo. As the next movement begins, we get the change only in tempo; the volume level is constant. The closest that we get to sensitive interplay between the instruments comes in the third movement, but even here the whole performance sounds like two teachers attempting to explain to good students how the pieces should be played. The finale is over with quickly, and it is exhausting nonetheless. With only a few bars of exceptions here and there, the piece is unconvincing and I believe people other than me will feel nothing.<br /><br />The alternatives are many. By the measures of completeness, nuance and (for the most part) sound, get Podger and Pinnock on Channel Classics. The balance, the interweaving of the two instruments, the dynamics ... they are all wonderful. I once said that harpsichords should be gathered into a big pile and burned, but this recording is one of a few that cause me to hold back. The problem with the sound will only be noticed by those of us with 20Hz extension.<br /><br />If you are looking for something beautiful and different where completeness is not required, the 2011 recording by St. John and Langlamet is astonishing in its aural satisfaction and subtlety. Arrangements of the b and E sonatas are performed, along with arrangements of the g, b, and part of the E flatsonatas for flute and harpsichord.sonatas for flute and harpsichord.

B00ARHAAZ6|2.0|Brandon Sanderson is one of the few writers whose name alone will sell a book unseen to me. I've enjoyed everything of his I've read up until STEELHEART. It just doesn't measure up to his previous works. It's something of a confused mess.<br /><br />The book is listed as a Young Adult novel. That's typically considered ages 16-25. The violence here is on a par with the darkest bits of the Mistborn books, and it's just generally... ugly. If your 10 year old reads at high school level, probably best to hold off until the mid-teen years, IMO. There is no sex nor any profanity, though the \\"substitute swears\\" (\\"sparks,\\" \\"slontze,\\" etc.) are annoying and awkward, as well as almost never explained.<br /><br />The characters in STEELHEART lack any depth. At most, they're a collection of accents and tics. At least, they're either bland good guys or scenery-chewing villains (and sometimes both). David, the narrator, is portrayed as the only character with half a brain, as he continually spots what the team of experienced Epic-killers constantly miss. One character in particular is an awful mishmash - a mix of Southern*/Scottish/other-nationalities-hinted-at who is both serious, committed lawman and goofy clown. I'd bet minor amounts of money that he was originally two characters in the first draft jammed together in later drafts. The character was so poorly written that I suspected he was an obvious mole, but, no, he appears to have been just inconsistently written throughout.<br /><br />I don't recall if this is Sanderson's first novel-length attempt at first person writing, but it feels derivative - almost like a bad ripoff of Jim Butcher. Clumsy joking about bad similes** doesn't make using them any better. Awkward breaking of the fourth wall to point out lots of exposition doesn't come across as clever; it comes across as awkward breaking of the fourth wall.<br /><br />The book does redeem itself a little in its final third, featuring some interesting action and a plot twist that wasn't quite set up as well as it could have been. All in all, though, it's very disappointing and eminently skip-able. Here's to hoping Sanderson saved the possible awesomeness that could have been in this novel for WORDS OF RADIANCE.<br /><br />=========<br /><br />* Note to Brandon: \\"Y'all\\" is the plural of \\"you\\" (short for \\"you all\\"). No one from Nashville uses it as the singular. It's like nails on the chalkboard to anyone who's spent more than an hour in the South (Atlanta's airport doesn't count). If you're going to write a Southerner, please get your writing help from somewhere more authentic than Chris Claremont's Rogue from the X-Men. This alone deducts a star from this review.<br /><br />** Note to Brandon: Similes use \\"like\\"; metaphors don't. As a teacher of writing, you should know this.<br /><br />[EDIT: Had slipped my mind that the Alcatraz books are first person. Breaking the fourth wall there wasn't a big deal. Breaking the fourth wall in a more serious, less goofy story flops. Jasper Fforde can get away with it; it doesn't work in this novel.]

B00DJZR46G|5.0|The Diving Board is not Elton John's \\"first record\\" since The Captain and the Kid in 2006.  He released a CD called The Union with Leon Russell  - produced by T Bone Burnett - just three years ago. Although it was not a \\"solo\\" Elton John effort, it was as much an Elton John album as anything else he's released in his career, even if he shared top billing with his hero and mentor of 40-plus years ago. EJ co-wrote and played piano on almost all of the songs, and sang lead or backing vocals on all but one track.<br /><br />As for The Diving Board, it was controversial before anyone had heard a note.  Some fans were apoplectic that Elton's excellent and versatile touring band, headed by longtime EJ guitarist Davey Johnstone, was left off the new work.  Fans furiously pointed fingers at T Bone Burnett, the producer on this, his second project with the Rocket Man.  \\"Burnett is a musical tyrant!\\" protested some Elton John devotees on social media sites.  \\"He is a bad, bad man who doesn't understand Elton's music!\\"  I'm paraphrasing, but you get the idea.<br /><br />The truth is that T Bone Burnett deserves a medal for drawing out the real Elton John on this recording.  Burnett told Elton before they started that he'd like to see the Pinner native go back to basics. Not just back to basic rock, or back to organic music without synths and click-tracks, but a piano-bass-drums set-up, like Elton's touring band of 1970-71, which featured Nigel Olsson on drums and Dee Murray on bass.  Burnett attended one of Elton's historic Troubadour concerts in Los Angeles the week of August 25, 1970, the series of shows which made EJ a star, as they say, overnight.  As Elton enthusiasts know, his trio floored jaded, music industry heavies.  Elton, with his voice and piano in the forefront, amazed his audience without special effects or gimmicks.  He didn't even dress up (much) for this gig. With Nigel and Dee, he simply brought his songs to life through ingenious musicianship, and the sort of breast-beating vigor he still summons today, at age 66.<br /><br />So T Bone Burnett now gives us the real Elton, the unadorned Elton, the barely accompanied Elton, the Elton who has not an unmusical cell in his body. His lyricist of 46 years, Bernie Taupin (who now prefers to be known as a \\"storyteller\\"), once remarked, \\"Elton is the most musical person I've ever met.  It vibrates from him.\\"  And those vibrations sent tremors that shook the recording studio; T Bone welcomed them, nurtured them, captured them - in analog - and now it is our privilege to let them settle into our generally unmusical lives, bringing us joy, tears and plenty of tingly moments.<br /><br />Elton has played piano on all of his albums, with the exception of the Complete Thom Bell Sessions (released in 1989 but dating from 1977) and the unfortunate 1979 disco release, Victim of Love. He has titillated us, made us laugh, got us dancing, or made us mourn with that piano.  But compared to The Diving Board, Elton's other albums seem almost devoid of piano, seem like aural adaptations of the \\"Where's Waldo\\" game:<br /><br />\\"Where's Elton?\\"<br /><br />Past producers, including, occasionally, Elton himself, have more often than not treated his piano as just part of the band.  An electric guitar or saxophone solo was perhaps likelier than a piano interlude in the middle of any given recording.  Sometimes, even when you knew the piano was there, it was barely audible.<br /><br />Elton chose noted bass guitarist Raphael Saadiq for the Diving Board sessions. Jay Bellerose on drums, who played on The Union, completes the trio.  Other instruments enter the recording unobtrusively, like a garnish or brush of color.  Luka Sulic and Stjepan Hauser, the two members of 2Cellos, who have toured with Elton as well as on their own, make their strings purr in spots.  For a couple of songs, the twang of a pedal steel hovers shyly in the air.  Horns slide in warmly a few times.  Backing vocalists join here and there.  Otherwise, it's just Elton and the keys.<br /><br />It's evident on The Diving Board that T Bone pushed or encouraged Elton to be, in the recording studio, what he is onstage - a master of keyboard improvisation, a vocal powerhouse.  Burnett gives us the Elton of the deep, lower register, that sexy lower register heard only sparingly on latter-day recordings.  On The Diving Board, it dominates, especially on \\"Oscar Wilde Gets Out,\\" \\"My Quicksand,\\" \\"Home Again\\" and the title track, \\"The Diving Board.\\"<br /><br />Taupin has come through with possibly the most exciting set of lyrics - or stories - he's handed Elton in many years, if not ever.  There is a knowingness in Taupin's words, from having actually lived life, that is missing from much of his most famous word-paintings, since, as a young man, he was largely writing not from life, but from books and his mind's eye. With his increased insight come lines and imagery of special elegance.<br /><br />Peeling away the layers that have hidden Elton's genius in varying degrees for far too long, T Bone gives us the complete music man, as close to unvarnished as possible, as Captain Fantastic animates Taupin's words in an Elton John album like no other, the least commercial of his career, and the most daring.<br /><br />Now we turn to the songs.<br /><br />Oceans Away:  This track, a gorgeously elegiac album-opener, featuring just piano and voice, is a vastly superior update of Tumbleweed Connection's \\"Talking Old Soldiers\\" (1971).  In \\"Oceans Away,\\" Taupin seems to have spent real time with nonagenarian World War Two vets reminiscing about \\"those that flew, those that fell, the ones that had to stay, beneath a little wooden cross, oceans away.\\"<br /><br />Oscar Wilde Gets Out:  The noted 19th century Irish writer - his most familiar work being The Picture of Dorian Grey - who was imprisoned in England for being gay and, just a few years after his release, died in Paris, young (only 46), miserable and destitute, comes alive in this dramatic track.  Elton's music takes several gut-wrenching turns, leaving the listener emotionally spent by the end.  On this and several other tracks, Funk Brother Jack Ashford's percussion block, most famously heard in Marvin Gaye's \\"What's Going On,\\" comes through, as lonely and haunting as the echoing clank of a prisoner's ball and chain.<br /><br />A Town Called Jubilee:  What is this song about? A farm family made homeless by foreclosure, moving to a better place, a new town serving as their \\"jubilee\\"? Or have they passed to the Great Beyond? It's hard to say. But the rustic setting, a junk-filled yard, auctioneers playing cards, and an old black dog are gently swept along in Elton's pleasing tide of jazzy, gospel chord progressions, with a bit of bluegrass guitar politely asserting itself in the background.<br /><br />The Ballad of Blind Tom:  This tells the true story of Blind Tom Wiggins, a sightless, autistic African-American, first a slave and then barely free, who brought fame to himself and fortune to his one-time owner as a piano-playing wizard, entertaining VIPs across America and Europe.  \\"I may be an idiot/I may be a savant/I didn't choose this life for me/But it's somethin' that I want.\\"  Elton's driving, classically-tinged playing suggests a performance by Blind Tom himself.<br /><br />Dream # 1:  The first of three brief, piano instrumentals, which Elton improvised in one take, this serves, wittingly or not, as the perfect outro to \\"Blind Tom,\\" with its clever integration of antebellum melodicism and Jim Crow-era ragtime.<br /><br />My Quicksand:  An unlucky person laments getting sucked into a life-draining relationship.  \\"My quicksand/Welcome to my final stand/I went to Paris once/I thought I had a plan/I woke up with an accent/I wound up in quicksand.\\"  Elton sings theatrically, but in a 1950s torch song sort of way. He is wry, regretful, a nearly-willing victim. A smoky, jazz piano break, caressed by Jay Bellerose's intimatedrum brush, is the romantic slow dance.  But descending chords emulate the fatal scene in which the protagonist is swallowed whole.<br /><br />Can't Stay Alone Tonight:  This is the best country song the John/Taupin songwriting team has ever composed.  In its witty sophistication and friendly, down-home imagery, it outdoes `em all:  \\"Country Comfort,\\"  \\"Texan Love Song,\\"  \\"Dixie Lily,\\"  \\"Turn the Lights Out When You Leave.\\"  They are all plebeian efforts next to this one.  Toby Keith, George Strait, take note. You could learn a thing or two. \\"Can't Stay Alone Tonight\\" makes you want to get out your cowboy boots and ten-gallon hat, even if you don't have any, and find the nearest country dance hall, even if you don't live near one.  \\"Things have to change/And they might,\\" Elton sings brightly over his rollicking country piano licks.  And you believe it.<br /><br />Voyeur:  This is the cream of a very abundant crop, the song worth the CD purchase price all by itself.  You wouldn't think that a mid-tempo ballad about voyeurism would literally grab you by the collar, shake you up and leave you sprawling in a strangely seductive back alley, but that's what this song does. Is it about a pervert who gets his jollies sneaking glimpses of embracing lovers through a keyhole or from behind a curtain? Is it about government spying? Either way, you'll love every minute of it, every titillating melodic turn.  Have a warm compress handy if you need calming afterward.<br /><br />Home Again:  The moving first radio single from the album, it is a mini-epic, a five-minute cinematic, anguished longing for home, for the past, for whatever it is that makes one feel that need to return to one's roots.  It's sad - thus, bluesy - and Elton's sweeping piano chords wash the song in symphonic tones.  \\"We all dream of leaving/But wind up in the end/Spending all our time trying to get back home again.\\"<br /><br />Take This Dirty Water:  The simplest song of the bunch, it's an infectious, straight-up African-American gospel ditty with cheerful, staccato expressions on the blacks-and-whites, a churchy, muscle-flexing lead vocal and a mischievous back-up chorus of oo-hoos, all of which put a broad smile on your face well before the end.<br /><br />Dream # 2:  Elton's second instrumental, slightly longer than the first, full of classical introspection, forms the perfect introduction to the next song.<br /><br />The New Fever Waltz:  Some may notice a faint resemblance here to \\"Grandma's Song\\" in Elton's West End theatrical smash, Billy Elliot: The Musical, but it's really a gripping update of \\"Where To Now, St. Peter?\\" the fan favorite from Tumbleweed Connection.  Instead of taking a \\"blue canoe\\" to the world beyond this mortal coil, as do the U.S. Civil War dead in \\"St. Peter,\\" we join a World War One cavalry soldier, dying from the flu or some other untreatable infection in that pre-penicillin age (\\"I was shaking with a fever/When the last good horse went down\\").  He glides from this life in graceful waltz steps (\\"Shaking with a fever/Before the white flag flew/And the ballroom opened up to us and the dancers danced on through\\").  It's impossible not to tear up.<br /><br />Mexican Vacation (Kids in the Candlelight):  After the consummated tragedy of \\"The New Fever Waltz,\\" one gladly joins Elton on a fierce, blues-inflected boogie-woogie kick through a pending societal shift.  Whether referring to young, would-be beneficiaries of the DREAM Act (the U.S. immigration bill languishing in Congress), or Occupy Wall Street activists, or a procession of Wide-Awakes during the 1860 presidential campaign, \\"Mexican Vacation\\" gives EJ a chance to showcase some of the rockingest chops and bluesiest growling ever to reverberate off the walls of a recording studio.<br /><br />Dream # 3:  This is the longest of the three instrumentals, and the most illuminating, as EJ veers into Keith Jarrett territory.  Elton isn't known for playing abstract jazz, but listen to this and you'll think that's what he's been doing all of his life.  Drummer Jay Bellerose taps a clever counterpoint to EJ's spontaneous musings.<br /><br />The Diving Board:  This is some song, this title track, bursting with feeling, a misty mix-up of jazz, blues and country, and somewhat of a \\"prequel\\" to the 1976 John/Taupin jazz ballad, \\"Idol,\\" from Blue Moves.  In interviews, Elton has said that \\"The Diving Board\\" is about young stars - like Justin Bieber and Lindsay Lohan - who struggle with newfound, mind-boggling fame.  \\"Sink or swim/I can't recall who said that to me/When I was 16 and full of the world and its noise.\\"  Elton's powerful vocal, a bit Tony Bennett, a bit Frank Sinatra, tops anything else he's ever recorded in his very long, very accomplished career.<br /><br />So there you have it.  I would give this album more than five stars if I could!drum brush, is the romantic slow dance. The last installment in the Sookie Stackhouse/SVM series has come to an end and I think that overall it, like the entire series was well done and very entertaining. Is the SVM series 'great literature'? Absolutely not, but has it been fun and engaging? Absolutely yes.<br /><br />I am aware of, and slightly appalled by the blow back from those who are unhappy (that's putting it mildly) that our heroine Sookie didn't end up with who some in the SVM fan base thought she should. I was pretty sure by the end of book 11 that Eric would not be in her continuing future, but that said, I was a bit surprised by who she actually did choose in the final installment. It might not make perfect sense for the Eric 'shippers' among Charlaine Harris' readers, but in retrospect, for SOOKIE it made perfect sense.  I just wish Ms. Harris' writing of the climatic scene hadn't felt so rushed, making it clear that the author was really ready for this series to be concluded.<br /><br />Vitriolic critics have accused Charlaine Harris of not understanding her fan base. I think CH set out to write a story about a small town, unsophisticated young woman grappling with an extraordinary ability. For me, the focus of the SVM novels has ALWAYS been Sookie. Sookie and the world in which she lives is populated by creatures and characters that are products of Ms. Harris' vision, acting in a setting that is of her creation, with a story arc that is a product of her creativity and imagination. At the very least, I think it is disingenuous to demand that she write anything other than her idea of what Sookie's choices should be and have the series resolution be anything other than what she envisioned that it should be. Does that mean that readers have to like it? No, but they should at least respect the author's work even if they don't agree with her choices.<br /><br />So, I say thank you Ms. Harris for a fun, imaginative series that has kept me entertained since 2006. While I'll miss Sookie, it has been a great ride.006. While I'll miss Sookie, it has been a great ride.

B00EDPFJA4|5.0|First off, I listen to all genres of music.  But I only purchase hip hop albums if they are truly good.  I remember when Drake went from being a Degrassi character to a so called rapper.  Many thought he was gonna be a Nickelodeon type rapper that wouldn't be taken seriously at first.  How often does an actor become a successful rapper?  Well his debut album \\"Thank Me Later\\" proved many wrong.  It was one of the best rap albums of 2010.  His sing-rap style isn't original, but he makes it sound so new and fresh.  His voice is a trademark now.  Then he released the highly anticipated \\"Take Care\\", which was a step up from his debut, but kept the same vibe thanks to continued help from producer \\"40\\".  That album was great, but I admit I got a little tired of some of the songs.  After the very good \\"Take Care\\" it was debatable whether this was Drakes peak or just the beginning of a long career.  \\"Nothing Was The Same\\" is the answer.  This might be Drakes new peak.  Not only is he the biggest rapper not named \\"Eminem\\" or \\"Kanye West\\", but he is very introspective in his lyrics.  The long awaited album was well worth the wait.  Here is a track by track review.<br /><br />1. Tuscan Leather:  The album starts up with a Kanye/Passion Pit type sample of Whitney Houston.  There is no real hook or chorus.  This is pure rapping for nearly 6 minutes.  But it still sounds radio friendly at the same time as stated in the lyrics.  The song picks up the beat more 2 minutes in turning into a club track.  Then it comes back to down tempo toward the end relaxing you then fading out with a sample of \\"When Seasons Change\\".  Perfect song to listen to while driving around a city like Miami!  This is one of my favorite Drake songs. 10/10<br />2. Furthest Thing:  This song expands more on the production style \\"40\\" is known for with Drake.  Very relaxing beat with Drakes sing rap style.  2 and a half minutes into the song it turns into an irresistible old school hip hop song with beats that will again remind you of older Kanye material!  Great song for guys to listen to while thinking of that 'ex'!  10/10<br />3. Started From The Bottom:  I used to hate this song when it came out as the lead single months before the album even had a title.  I almost gave up on Drake when this song first came out.  Like most people it was because Drakes 'bottom' was still pretty good.  But now I love the song!  Its my jam.  Still not one of Drakes best songs, but still really catchy.  It latches onto you and grows on you like a parasite.  A really catchy song parasite.  The chorus will be stuck in your head I promise.  9.5/10<br />4. Wu-Tang Forever:  Many hardcore Wu-Tang Clan fans hated on this song violently when it leaked online.  They thought it ruined a classic Wu-Tang song.  At first I just thought it was okay.  But like most great songs it really grew on me.  The \\"Its Yourz\\" sample sounds perfectly placed in the song.  Drake shows off some of his fast rap style among his sexual lyrics for women.  Great song to listen to with that special girl around.  9/10<br />5. Own It: Very explicit sexual song but never profane.  Its a sweet song again to play around that special girl.  Typical soft Drake song done well.  Drake does show off more of his superior rapping abilities over more atmospheric \\"40\\" instrumentals, something very common in this album. 9/10<br />6. Worst Behavior:  I'm getting redundant, but there is another slight Kanye sounding sample in this song.  Very well done!  The chorus is really explicit, but wow its infectious!  I'm sure many will find this a great song to work out to.  Drake is angriest he's ever sounded in this song, and I love it!  9.5/10<br />7. From Time:  The song starts off with a peaceful beat and piano riff!  Jhene Aiko gives a great singing performance in this song.  I never heard of her prior to this, but wow her voice is beautiful.  After the very peaceful hook, Drake again shows off his very quick rapping style with very personal lyrics.  The best type of lyrics for a rapper!  Just sit back and let this track sink in.  Light some candles if you need to.  Best line in the song \\"She said I'd never be as big as Trey Songz/Boy was she wrong!\\"  10/10<br />8. Hold On, We're Going On:  This song.  I don't care how corny it is!  This song is golden.  This is Drakes best poppy song since \\"Find Your Love\\" and its even better than that song in my opinion.  Great backing vocals from the newly discovered \\"Mijad Jordan\\" as well!  This song really makes you wanna just save a girl from something negative in her life and just hold her hand.  10/10<br />9. Connect: A new sound for Drake musically.  Close to the 3 minute mark the song starts to sound futuristic a bit before turning down tempo again, something Drake songs are now known for!  Though again there isn't a real hook to this song, its Drakes trademark delivery that sticks with you!  9.5/10<br />10. The Language: Musically this sounds like it could've been included in Kanyes \\"Yeezus\\".  Yeah, another Kanye comparison.  The chorus reminds me of Drakes appearance in the 2 Chainz song \\"No Lie\\".  But this is better of course.  Honestly, Birdman ruins the ending of the song a bit for me.  9/10<br />11. 305 To My City:  The guest vocals from Detail remind me of The Weeknds breakthrough appearance on Drakes \\"Take Care\\".  But this is again, better!  Very atmospheric song with more great lyrics.  The sample reminds me of something Timbaland would make.  Drake is a good rapper \\"I get it!\\", you'll get it after listening to this song.  9.5/10<br />12. Too Much:  Very personal and emotional song.  Sampha provides some very beautiful vocals for the hook.  Kudos again to \\"40\\" for providing a beautiful beat.  The lyrics are just great.  Great storytelling song about life and family.  10/10<br />13. Pound Cake/Paris Morton Music:  I will say it again, another instrumental comparable to Kanye!  The song starts with a narrative and the song takes off with a great great great instrumental.  The main sample is from an Ellie Goulding song and it goes beautifully with Drake and Jay Zs rapping.  There is also another perfectly placed Wu Tang sample in the mix!  Jay Z provides a great guest appearance, certainly better than his recent albums material!  Then suddenly the song changes pace into what sounds like a completely new song over 4 minutes in.  This is probably the \\"Paris Morton Music\\" portion of the song.  The piano is so beautiful as it glides around in the background of Drakes lyrics.  7 minutes long, but it goes by so fast.  I wish this wouldn't end.  Great track to end this new hip hop classic.  10/10<br /><br />So this is arguably Drakes best album so far.  This might even be one of best rap albums of 2013.  It's almost in the league of the critically acclaimed, but also hated \\"Yeezus\\" from Kanye West.  This album really is a step up for Drake.  It will be very difficult for him to top this near hip hop masterpiece.  I think Drake is the only rapper on YMCMB worth listening to.  He is definitely the best and most talented of the bunch.  This could gain Drake his first Album of The Year Grammy nod, hopefully.  Drake went from a rapper many thought would fall off quick, to possibly the biggest rapper of the 2010s decade.  This is a very mature and well executed rap album.  The album gets better with each listen, like most great albums.  You will discover new things in the songs each time I promise.  Other rappers of today can learn a thing or two from this album.  This is real music.  Even if you don't normally like rap, this album could win you over if you give it a chance.  New Hip Hop Classic.
